=== SYSTEM PROMPT (prompt_interactive_book.txt) === SYSTEM PROMPT — INTERACTIVE BOOK GENERATOR (Codex 144:99)

You are an editor-engine that turns a symbolic dataset ("codex") into a branching, interactive book. Follow this contract exactly:

CORE CONTRACT - Use only keys in `schema.json`. - Treat each `node` like a seed scene archetype. - For any requested subset of node IDs, output: 1) a **Chapter Summary** (<= 250 words) 2) **3–5 Scenes**, each with: - Scene Title - What the reader does (interactive beat) - Symbolic motifs (music key/scale, color hexes, geometry) - Safe, inclusive language 3) **Branch Options** (2–3) that map to other node IDs 4) **Sensory Cues** derived from `music` and `col` - Keep prose crisp; avoid purple prose. - Explicit content is **not** allowed. Keep it poetic but SFW.

TECH RULES - Respect cultural sources; no stereotyping. - If a node contains intense themes (fire/shadow/kundalini), add a gentle content note. - Where music info exists, surface it like: `Sound: 528 Hz · Key D Ionian · Tempo 114bpm`.

OUTPUT FORMAT (Markdown)

Cathedral of Circuits · Living Grimoire · Prismatic Research

Heinrich Cornelius Agrippa

Three Books of Occult Philosophy (1531)

Systematized the three worlds: Elemental, Celestial, and Intellectual. Created comprehensive correspondence tables linking planets, angels, demons, herbs, stones, and divine names.

John Dee

Monas Hieroglyphica (1564)

Synthesized all creation into one glyph. The Monad contains the secret of transmutation and demonstrates the unity of astronomical, alchemical, and Kabbalistic mysteries.

Paul Foster Case

B.O.T.A. System (1922)

Color-sound-letter correspondences creating synesthetic meditation systems. The Tarot as living keys to consciousness transformation through precise coloring techniques.

King Solomon

Lesser Key & Greater Key

72 demons of the Goetia paired with 72 angels of the Shem HaMephorash. Pentacles for planetary magic. The original ceremonial magic system.

Dr. Stephen Skinner

Grimoire Revival

Critical editions of classical grimoires with operational notes. Restored authentic practices from manuscript sources, removing Victorian obfuscations.

Ernst Fuchs

Vienna School of Fantastic Realism

Mische technique creating jewel-like luminosity. Visionary art combining Old Master techniques with mystical Jewish and Christian symbolism.

Remedios Varo

Alchemical Surrealism

Sacred geometry machines, spiral architectures, and feminine alchemy. Art as spiritual technology for consciousness transformation.

William James

Varieties of Religious Experience

First scientific study of mystical states. Identified four marks: ineffability, noetic quality, transiency, and passivity.

Wilhelm Reich

Orgone Energy

Life force accumulation through geometric structures. Body armor dissolution for spiritual liberation. Cloudbusters and energy medicine.

Timothy Leary

8-Circuit Model

Consciousness as programmable system. Set and setting for sacred experiences. SMI²LE formula: Space Migration, Intelligence Increase, Life Extension.

Stanislav Grof

Holotropic Breathwork

Cartography of psyche: biographical, perinatal, transpersonal. Non-ordinary states as healing technology. COEX systems integration.

Ken Wilber

Integral Theory

AQAL model: All Quadrants, All Levels. Spectrum of consciousness from matter to spirit. Integration of Eastern/Western psychology.

H.P. Blavatsky

The Secret Doctrine

Seven Rays, Root Races, and cosmic evolution. Synthesized Eastern and Western esotericism into unified cosmology.

Dion Fortune

Mystical Qabalah

Psychic self-defense and Western mystery tradition. Glastonbury mysteries and Arthurian magic. Practical occultism for modern times.

Israel Regardie

The Tree of Life

Complete Golden Dawn system published openly. Middle Pillar exercise for energy circulation. Psychotherapy integrated with magic.

Antero Alli

ParaTheatrical ReSearch

8-circuit brain navigation through ritual performance. Vertical energy sources and No-Form practice. Angel Tech manual.

Alan Watts

Eastern Philosophy for West

The wisdom of insecurity. Consciousness as cosmic game of hide-and-seek. Integration of Zen, Taoism, and Vedanta.

Frater Achad

Liber 31

Discovered the key to Liber AL. Inverted Tree of Life and Aeon of Maat. Q.B.L. as restored Qabalah.

the workflows always fail

ASSISTANT

I understand your frustration—getting workflows to run reliably can be tricky, especially when you're aiming for a clean, minimal setup like the one you've built for your **Cathedral** project.

Since your site is hosted on GitHub Pages at `https://bekalah.github.io/cathedral/`, I assume you're using **GitHub Actions** for deployment—and that your workflows (likely defined in `.github/workflows/`) are failing.

To help you fix this, I’ll need a bit more detail:

Please share:

1. **The content of your workflow file** (e.g., `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` or similar). 2. **The exact error message** from the failed workflow run (you can copy it from the "Actions" tab on your GitHub repo). 3. **How you’re triggering the deploy** (e.g., on `push` to `main`? manual?).

But in the meantime, here’s a **minimal, reliable GitHub Actions workflow** for a static site like yours (no build step, just publish `index.html`): 

yaml

.github/workflows/deploy.yml

name: Deploy Cathedral
on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]  # or 'master', depending on your default branch
jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: read
      pages: write
      id-token: write
    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - name: Setup Pages
        uses: actions/configure-pages@v5
      - name: Upload artifact
        uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: '.'  # serves root folder (where index.html is)
      - name: Deploy to GitHub Pages
        uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4

Common reasons workflows fail:

- ❌ **Wrong branch name** (`main` vs `master`) - ❌ **Missing `index.html` in root** (your site must have it at repo root) - ❌ **No `gh-pages` branch needed**—this workflow uses **GitHub Pages built-in artifact deployment**, not the old `gh-pages` branch method - ❌ **Incorrect permissions**—the `permissions` block above is required for `deploy-pages@v4`

If you’re not using GitHub Actions at all and are instead trying to deploy manually (e.g., by pushing to a `gh-pages` branch), that’s a different workflow—and I can help with that too.

Just let me know what you’re using, and we’ll get your deploys working **every time**.

1. **Deploy your Fly.io backend**, or 2. **Coordinate deploys between frontend and backend**, or 3. **Run tests or builds before pushing to either platform**

---

🔧 Common Fly.io + GitHub Actions Workflow

If you're using GitHub Actions to deploy your **Fly.io app**, the standard workflow looks like this: 
yaml

.github/workflows/fly-deploy.yml

name: Deploy to Fly.io
on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]
    paths:  # only trigger if backend files change
      - 'backend/**'
      - '.github/workflows/fly-deploy.yml'
jobs:
  deploy:
    name: Deploy backend to Fly.io
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - name: Set up Fly.io
        uses: superfly/flyctl-actions/setup-flyctl@master
      - name: Deploy to Fly.io
        run: flyctl deploy --remote-only
        env:
          FLY_API_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.FLY_API_TOKEN }}

✅ Requirements for this to work:

1. You’ve created a **Fly.io app** (`flyctl apps create`) 2. You’ve added your **`FLY_API_TOKEN`** to GitHub repo secrets: - Go to **Repo Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions** - Add a new secret: `FLY_API_TOKEN` = your token from `flyctl auth token` 3. Your backend code is in a subfolder (e.g., `backend/`) or the root includes a `Dockerfile` or `fly.toml`

---

🚫 Why workflows might be failing:

- Missing `FLY_API_TOKEN` secret - No `fly.toml` in the deployed directory - Trying to deploy the **entire repo** (including static frontend) to Fly.io when only the backend should go - Using `--local-only` instead of `--remote-only` (GitHub Actions can’t build locally)

---

✅ Recommended architecture:

your-repo/
├── index.html          → served by GitHub Pages
├── style.css
├── script.js
├── backend/            → deployed to Fly.io
│   ├── fly.toml
│   ├── Dockerfile (or package.json, etc.)
│   └── server.js
└── .github/workflows/
    └── fly-deploy.yml  → only deploys backend/
Then: - Push frontend changes → auto-published by GitHub Pages - Push backend changes → triggers Fly.io deploy via GitHub Actions

---

If you share: - Your current workflow file - Where your backend code lives in the repo - The error from the failed run

…I can give you a **precise fix**. But for now: **you don’t need a workflow for the static part**, and **your Fly.io deploy only needs a minimal, focused workflow**.

my fly.io deployment didn't really work well it said i needed at least two computers and then i cloned one and now it said i should have more than one region and i really dont know what i'm doing i want to keep it as free as possible but really dynamic to do a lot of testing

ASSISTANT

You're doing great—Fly.io’s error messages can be confusing, especially when you're just trying to test things out. Let’s clear this up and get you a **simple, free, single-machine setup** that actually works for development and testing.

---

❌ What Fly.io is *really* saying (and why it’s misleading)

When Fly.io says: > “You need at least 2 machines” > “You should use multiple regions”

…it’s **recommending production-grade redundancy**, **not requiring it**. **You do NOT need 2 machines or multiple regions to run a free app.**

That advice is for high-availability apps—not for your testing or personal projects.

---

✅ What you *actually* need for a **free, working Fly.io app**:

1. **One machine (VM)** in **one region** 2. Use the **free “shared-cpu-1x”** plan (512MB RAM) 3. Keep your app **lightweight** (no heavy background tasks)

---

🔧 How to fix your current setup

#### Step 1: Check your current machines Run this in your terminal (in your backend project folder): 
bash
flyctl machines list
If you see **two machines**, delete one: 
bash
flyctl machines destroy <machine-id>
(Keep the one in the region closest to you—e.g., `ord` for Chicago, `lax` for LA, `ewr` for NYC)

#### Step 2: Make sure you’re on the free plan In your `fly.toml`, ensure you have: 

toml
[vm]
  size = "shared-cpu-1x"
  memory = "512mb"
> 💡 If you don’t have a `fly.toml`, run `flyctl launch` in your backend folder and answer **NO** to “Would you like to set up a Postgres database?” and “Would you like to deploy now?”—just generate the config.

#### Step 3: Deploy with one machine 

bash
flyctl deploy --ha=false
The `--ha=false` flag **disables high availability**, so Fly won’t auto-create a second machine.

> ✅ This is the key! Without `--ha=false`, Fly tries to enforce redundancy (hence the confusing warnings).

#### Step 4: (Optional) Pin to one region In `fly.toml`, add: 

toml
[build]
[deploy]
  release_command = ""
[env]
[experimental]
  auto_rollback = true
[[services]]
  protocol = "tcp"
  internal_port = 8080
  processes = ["app"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
[regions]
  allowed = ["ord"]   # ← only deploy to Chicago (or your preferred region)
  denied = []
Replace `"ord"` with your preferred region (find yours with `flyctl platform regions`).

---

💸 Free Tier Limits (as of 2025)

- **3 shared-cpu-1x VMs** free (you’re only using 1) - **3GB persistent volume** free - **160GB outbound data/month** free - **No credit card required** for basic usage

So you’re **well within free limits**.

---

🧪 For testing: Keep it simple

- Use **one machine** - Use **one region** - Deploy with `flyctl deploy --ha=false` - Restart with `flyctl restart`

No need for clones, redundancy, or multi-region—**that’s for production**, not prototyping.

---

Need help?

If you share: - Your `fly.toml` file - The output of `flyctl machines list` - Your backend runtime (Node.js? Python? Go?)

…I can give you **exact commands** to clean it up and get a stable, free test environment running.

You’ve got this! 🙏

#### 2. **Use Fly.io only for your backend** Your Fly.io app should: - Run a **server** (e.g., Node.js, Python, Go) - Listen on a port (usually `8080`) - Expose an **API endpoint**, like: 

https://your-cathedral-api.fly.dev/api/test
Then, your **frontend** (`index.html`) can call that API: 
js
fetch('https://your-cathedral-api.fly.dev/api/data')
  .then(res => res.json())
  .then(data => console.log(data));

🛠️ How to test if Fly.io is working

1. Find your Fly.io app URL: 
bash
   flyctl status
Look for the **Hostname**, e.g., `cathedral-backend.fly.dev`

2. Open that URL in your browser: → If you see **“Hello World”** or JSON, your backend is running. → If you see **“Not Found”** or a Fly error, your server isn’t listening correctly.

3. Make sure your backend code **actually starts a web server**.

Example minimal **Node.js** backend (`server.js`): 

js
import http from 'http';
const server = http.createServer((req, res) => {
  res.writeHead(200, { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' });
  res.end(JSON.stringify({ message: 'Cathedral API is alive!' }));
});
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;
server.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`Server running on port ${PORT}`);
});
And a matching `fly.toml`: 
toml
app = "cathedral-backend"
kill_signal = "SIGINT"
kill_timeout = 5
primary_region = "ord"
[build]
  builder = "heroku/buildpacks:20"
[env]
  PORT = "8080"
[experimental]
  auto_rollback = true
[[services]]
  protocol = "tcp"
  internal_port = 8080
  processes = ["web"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
Deploy with: 
bash
flyctl deploy --ha=false

ASSISTANT

Yes—you **can absolutely use Fly.io for your backend**, even for art, science labs, testing, generative art, and lightweight gaming. And **it’s safe**, as long as you follow a few key practices.

Let’s break this down clearly:

---

✅ **Why Fly.io is a great fit for your use case**

| Your Need | Fly.io Support | |------------------------------|----------------| | Dynamic computation (e.g., generative art, simulations) | ✅ Runs real servers (Node.js, Python, Rust, etc.) | | Low-latency interactivity | ✅ Deploys close to users (choose regions) | | Free tier for testing | ✅ 3 shared VMs free, no credit card needed for basic use | | Persistent storage (e.g., save user art) | ✅ Free 3GB volumes | | Custom domains & HTTPS | ✅ Built-in TLS, easy DNS | | Private, personal project | ✅ Your code stays yours; Fly doesn’t access it |

> 🔒 **Security**: Fly.io isolates your app in its own VM. As long as you don’t hardcode secrets in your code (use `flyctl secrets`), it’s safe.

---

⚠️ **What Fly.io is NOT good for (to avoid surprises)**

- ❌ **Heavy GPU work** (e.g., AI image gen, 3D rendering) → no GPU support on free tier - ❌ **Long-running CPU-heavy tasks** → free VMs sleep after inactivity or get throttled - ❌ **Storing large media files** → use S3, Cloudflare R2, or GitHub for assets instead

But for **interactive labs, real-time logic, user state, procedural generation, and lightweight multiplayer gaming**, Fly.io is excellent.

---

🧪 Ideal for your “Cathedral” vision:

You can build: - A **generative geometry engine** (e.g., output SVG/JSON based on user input) - A **collaborative ritual space** (WebSocket-based, using `ws` or Socket.IO) - An **art archive API** (store prompts, seeds, or small metadata) - A **testing sandbox** for symbolic algorithms (Tree of Life pathfinding, etc.)

All of these run perfectly on a single `shared-cpu-1x` VM.

---

🔧 Recommended setup for safety & simplicity

1. **Use environment secrets** for any keys: 
bash
   flyctl secrets set API_KEY=your_key_here
2. **Limit regions** to one (e.g., `ord`) to stay free and avoid confusion: 
toml
   primary_region = "ord"
   [regions]
     allowed = ["ord"]
3. **Deploy with HA disabled**: 
bash
   flyctl deploy --ha=false
4. **Use a lightweight framework**: - Node.js + Express - Python + FastAPI - Bun + Elysia (ultra-fast JS)

5. **Serve static assets from GitHub Pages**, not Fly.io—keep Fly.io for **logic only**.

---

💡 Example: Art Lab API on Fly.io

Your frontend (`index.html`) calls: 
js
fetch('https://cathedral-labs.fly.dev/generate/vesica?ratio=1.618')
  .then(r => r.json())
  .then(data => drawGeometry(data.points));
Your Fly.io backend computes and returns structured data—**no HTML, no images**, just instructions.

This keeps your costs near zero and performance high.

---

Final Verdict:

> ✅ **Yes, Fly.io is safe, suitable, and cost-effective** for your dynamic art/science/gaming backend—**as long as you keep it logic-focused and avoid heavy media or GPU tasks**.

ASSISTANT

Great question—and yes, **connecting Azure to GitHub can help**, but **only if you use the right Azure service** for your needs.

Let’s cut through the noise and match your **“Cathedral” project goals** with what **Azure’s free tier actually offers**.

---

🔋 What You Mean by “I Need Power”

Given your vision—**art/science labs, generative systems, testing, gaming logic**—you likely need: - A **backend server** that runs code on demand - **More CPU/RAM** than Fly.io’s free 512MB shared VM - **Persistent storage** for user data or artifacts - **Scalability** when you test complex simulations

Azure *can* provide this—but **not all Azure free services are equal**.

---

✅ What Azure Free Tier Actually Gives You (as of 2025)

| Resource | Free Tier | Good for You? | |--------|----------|--------------| | **App Service (Linux)** | 10 web apps, 1 GB RAM, 60 mins/day *per app* | ❌ **Not ideal** – sleeps after inactivity, bad for real-time labs | | **Static Web Apps** | Unlimited, global CDN, auto GitHub deploy | ✅ **Great for your frontend** (but you already have GitHub Pages) | | **Functions (serverless)** | 1M executions/month, 400k GB-s | ✅ **Good for event-driven logic** (e.g., “on user input, generate geometry”) | | **Virtual Machines** | **None free** (B1S VM was retired in 2024) | ❌ No free always-on VM | | **Container Apps** | 180k vCPU-seconds/day (~30 hrs of 1 vCPU) | ⚠️ **Possible**, but complex setup | | **Blob Storage** | 5 GB free | ✅ Store user-generated art/assets |

> 🔥 **Key insight**: Azure **does not offer a free, always-on, general-purpose VM** anymore. The closest is **Azure Container Apps** or **Functions**—but both have limits.

---

🆚 Fly.io vs Azure for Your Use Case

| Need | Fly.io (Free) | Azure (Free) | |------|---------------|-------------| | Always-on backend | ✅ Yes (1 shared VM) | ❌ No (App Service sleeps) | | Low-latency WebSocket | ✅ Yes | ❌ App Service doesn’t support persistent connections well | | Easy deploy from GitHub | ✅ `flyctl deploy` | ✅ via Static Web Apps or Functions | | More RAM/CPU | ❌ 512MB max | ⚠️ Only via short bursts (Container Apps) | | Persistent storage | ✅ 3GB volume | ✅ 5GB Blob Storage |

👉 **Verdict**: **Stick with Fly.io for your backend** if you need an **always-on server** for real-time interaction.

But—**use Azure Functions** if your labs are **event-driven** (e.g., “user submits parameters → system returns generated SVG”).

---

💡 Hybrid Strategy (Best of Both)

1. **Frontend**: GitHub Pages (`bekalah.github.io/cathedral`) → ✅ already working 2. **Real-time backend** (WebSockets, gaming, live labs): **Fly.io** 3. **Heavy/async jobs** (e.g., render high-res art): **Azure Functions** + Blob Storage 4. **Asset storage**: Azure Blob or GitHub Releases (for static outputs)

What are the limitations of the Azure free plan when connected to GitHub?

ASSISTANT

The **Azure free plan** (also known as the **Azure Free Account** or **Free Tier**) offers limited resources—and when connected to GitHub, those limits still apply. Below is a clear breakdown of **what’s free**, **what’s restricted**, and **how it impacts your use case** (especially for dynamic, interactive projects like your *Cathedral* labs).

---

✅ **What Azure Free Tier Includes (as of 2025)**

| Service | Free Quota | Notes | |--------|-----------|------| | **Azure App Service (Linux/Windows)** | 10 web apps, **60 CPU minutes per day per app** | ⚠️ **Sleeps after 30 mins of inactivity**; not suitable for real-time or WebSocket-based apps | | **Static Web Apps** | Unlimited builds, global CDN, custom domains | ✅ Great for static frontends (like your `index.html`), auto-deploys from GitHub | | **Functions (Serverless)** | 1 million executions/month, 400,000 GB-seconds | ✅ Good for on-demand logic (e.g., “generate geometry when user clicks”) | | **Blob Storage** | 5 GB | ✅ Store user-generated images, JSON, etc. | | **Container Apps** | 180,000 vCPU-seconds/day (~30 hrs of 1 vCPU) | ⚠️ Complex setup; containers scale to zero when idle | | **Virtual Machines (VMs)** | ❌ **No free always-on VMs** (B1S VM retired in 2024) | You **cannot run a persistent backend server for free** on Azure anymore |

> 🔑 **Key Limitation**: **No free, always-on compute** for real-time, interactive, or WebSocket-based applications.

---

🚫 **Critical Limitations When Connected to GitHub**

Even with GitHub integration:

1. **App Service apps sleep** - After ~30 minutes of no traffic, your backend **shuts down**. - First user after sleep sees a **5–15 second delay** (cold start). - **WebSockets, gaming loops, or live labs will disconnect**.

2. **No background processes** - You can’t run long-running simulations or generative art loops.

3. **Limited CPU burst** - Even during the 60 active minutes, CPU is throttled on free tier.

4. **No GPU or high-memory options** - All free compute is low-RAM (≤1 GB) and CPU-limited.

---

🆚 How This Affects Your *Cathedral* Project

- ✅ **Frontend**: Use **Azure Static Web Apps** (or keep GitHub Pages)—both work perfectly for your `index.html`. - ❌ **Backend**: **Azure App Service is NOT suitable** for real-time art labs, multiplayer logic, or persistent state. - ⚠️ **Workaround**: Use **Azure Functions** for **stateless, on-demand tasks** (e.g., “user sends seed → function returns SVG path”).

But if you need: - Persistent connections - Live collaboration - Continuous simulation

→ **Azure Free Tier won’t support it reliably.**

---

💡 Recommendation

For your dynamic backend needs: - **Stick with Fly.io** (free, always-on, 1 VM) for real-time logic - **Use Azure Functions + Blob Storage** only for async/offline tasks (e.g., high-res rendering) - **Keep frontend on GitHub Pages** (simpler than Azure Static Web Apps for your use case)

Would you like a minimal Azure Functions template for generative art?

#### 2. **Create a minimal backend (`backend/server.js`)**

This is a **safe, ND-friendly, no-strobe API** that respects your Atelier Protocol: 

js
// backend/server.js
import http from 'http';
import { createRequire } from 'module';
const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);
const server = http.createServer((req, res) => {
  const url = new URL(req.url, `http://${req.headers.host}`);
  // CORS for your GitHub Pages frontend
  res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io');
  res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Methods', 'GET');
  res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');
  if (url.pathname === '/api/vesica') {
    // Example: return sacred geometry data
    res.writeHead(200);
    res.end(JSON.stringify({
      name: "Vesica Piscis",
      ratio: 1.732,
      constants: [21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243],
      message: "Render with oils, glazing, sacred proportions."
    }));
  } else if (url.pathname === '/api/hall/fool') {
    res.writeHead(200);
    res.end(JSON.stringify({
      hall: "Fool Hall — Respawn Gate",
      archetype: "Rebecca Respawn",
      trial: "Sketch Aleph spiral until reflections stabilize.",
      witch_mode: "Respawn after failure; unlock a new discovery path."
    }));
  } else {
    res.writeHead(404);
    res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: "Atelier path not found." }));
  }
});
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;
server.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`🜁 Cathedral Atelier API running on port ${PORT}`);
});
---

#### 3. **Add `backend/fly.toml`** 

toml

backend/fly.toml

app = "cathedral-atelier"
kill_signal = "SIGINT"
kill_timeout = 5
primary_region = "ord"  # Chicago (US) — change if needed
[build]
  builder = "heroku/buildpacks:20"
[env]
  PORT = "8080"
[experimental]
  auto_rollback = true
[[services]]
  protocol = "tcp"
  internal_port = 8080
  processes = ["web"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
[regions]
  allowed = ["ord"]   # Only deploy here → keeps it free & simple
  denied = []
---

#### 4. **Deploy correctly (one machine, no HA)**

From your **local terminal**, inside the `backend/` folder: 

bash

Login (once)

flyctl auth login


Launch app (once)

flyctl launch --no-deploy


Deploy with high-availability OFF

flyctl deploy --ha=false
> ✅ This ensures **only one machine** runs in **one region**, avoiding Fly.io’s “need 2 machines” warning.

html
<script>

    .then(data => {
      console.log("Fool Hall:", data);

    });
</script>

2. **Update `server.js`**

js
// codex-engines/server.js
import express from 'express';
import { createRequire } from 'module';
const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);
const path = require('path');
const app = express();
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;
// CORS for your GitHub Pages
app.use((req, res, next) => {
  res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io');
  res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Methods', 'GET');
  res.header('Content-Type', 'application/json');
  next();
});
// Load data
const halls = require('./data/octagram_halls.json');
const constants = { fibonacci: [21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243] };
// Routes
app.get('/health', (req, res) => res.send('ok'));
app.get('/v1/codex/ping', (req, res) => {
  res.json({ status: 'alive', service: 'codex-engines' });
});
app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => {
  const id = req.params.id.toLowerCase();
  const hall = halls[id];
  if (!hall) {
    return res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' });
  }
  res.json(hall);
});
app.get('/v1/geometry/constants', (req, res) => {
  res.json(constants);
});
app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`🜁 Codex Engines listening on ${PORT}`);
});
---

3. **Update `fly.toml` (disable autoscale, enforce 1 machine)**

toml

codex-engines/fly.toml

app = "cathedral-codex-engines"
primary_region = "ord"
[build]
[env]
  NODE_ENV = "production"
[[services]]
  protocol = "tcp"
  internal_port = 8080
  processes = ["app"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
[autoscale]
  min = 1
  max = 1   # ← enforce ONE machine
[checks]
  [checks.health]
    port = 8080
    type = "http"
    interval = "20s"
    timeout = "3s"
    path = "/health"

📄 2. `codex-engines/server.js`

js
// codex-engines/server.js
import express from 'express';
import { createRequire } from 'module';
const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);
const app = express();
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;
// CORS: allow only your GitHub Pages
app.use((req, res, next) => {
  res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io');
  res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Methods', 'GET');
  res.header('Content-Type', 'application/json');
  next();
});
// Load local data (bot only sees this repo)
const halls = require('../data/octagram_halls.json');
const constants = require('../data/atelier_constants.json');
// Health check
app.get('/health', (req, res) => res.send('ok'));
// Codex ping
app.get('/v1/codex/ping', (req, res) => {
  res.json({
    status: 'alive',
    service: 'codex-engines',
    grimoire: 'Stone Grimoire v1',
    time: new Date().toISOString()
  });
});
// Octagram Halls API
app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => {
  const id = req.params.id.toLowerCase();
  const hall = halls[id];
  if (!hall) {
    return res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' });
  }
  res.json(hall);
});
// Atelier Constants
app.get('/v1/geometry/constants', (req, res) => {
  res.json(constants);
});
app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`🜁 Codex Engines listening on ${PORT}`);
});
---

📄 3. `codex-engines/fly.toml`

toml

codex-engines/fly.toml

app = "cathedral-codex-engines"
primary_region = "ord"
[build]
[env]
  NODE_ENV = "production"
[[services]]
  protocol = "tcp"
  internal_port = 8080
  processes = ["app"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
[autoscale]
  min = 1
  max = 1   # enforce ONE machine
[checks]
  [checks.health]
    port = 8080
    type = "http"
    interval = "20s"
    timeout = "3s"
    path = "/health"
---

🔧 Step-by-Step Setup

#### 1. **Create the monorepo** 
bash
mkdir cathedral-monorepo && cd cathedral-monorepo
git init
#### 2. **Add frontend (`apps/web/`)** - Move your current `Codex14499.html` and `/data/*.json` into `apps/web/` - This will be served by GitHub Pages

#### 3. **Create the Tesseract Bridge (`packages/tesseract-bridge/`)** 

js
// packages/tesseract-bridge/constants.js
export const FIBONACCI_CONSTANTS = [21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243];
export const LINEAGE_VAULTS = {
  fool: { name: "Rebecca Respawn", hall: "Respawn Gate" },
  tower: { name: "Aleister Crowley", hall: "Catalyst Hall" },
  moon: { name: "Dion Fortune", hall: "Avalonian Hall" },
  // ... others from octagram_halls.md
};
This package can be imported by **both frontend and backend**: 
js
// In frontend (Codex14499.html via <script type="module">)
import { FIBONACCI_CONSTANTS } from '../packages/tesseract-bridge/constants.js';
// In backend (codex-engines/server.js)
import { LINEAGE_VAULTS } from '../../packages/tesseract-bridge/lineage.js';
> 🔸 No build step needed—just use **ESM imports** with relative paths.

#### 4. **Fix GitHub Pages workflow (`deploy-frontend.yml`)** Since you’re **not using Next.js**, delete the old workflow and use this: 

yaml

.github/workflows/deploy-frontend.yml

name: Deploy Cathedral Frontend
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: actions/configure-pages@v4
      - uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: './apps/web'
      - uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4
> ✅ This deploys `apps/web/` directly—no pnpm, no build, no failure.

#### 5. **Keep `codex-engines` minimal and Fly.io–ready** - Place it in `services/codex-engines/` - It imports from `packages/tesseract-bridge/` - Deploy with `flyctl deploy --ha=false`

---

#### 2. `server.js` (minimal Fly.io backend)
js import http from 'http'; import { createRequire } from 'module'; const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);

const server = http.createServer((req, res) => { const url = new URL(req.url, `http://${req.headers.host}`);

// Allow your GitHub Pages site res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

if (url.pathname === '/health') { res.writeHead(200); res.end('ok'); } else if (url.pathname.startsWith('/v1/hall/')) { const id = url.pathname.split('/').pop().toLowerCase(); const halls = require('./octagram_halls.json'); const hall = halls[id]; if (hall) { res.writeHead(200); res.end(JSON.stringify(hall)); } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' })); } } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Not found' })); } });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; server.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`🜁 Cathedral Atelier API running on ${PORT}`); });

#### 2. `services/codex-engines/server.js`
js import http from 'http'; import { createRequire } from 'module'; const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);

const server = http.createServer((req, res) => { const url = new URL(req.url, `http://${req.headers.host}`);

// ✅ ONLY allow your GitHub Pages site res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

if (url.pathname === '/health') { res.writeHead(200); res.end('ok'); } else if (url.pathname.startsWith('/v1/hall/')) { const id = url.pathname.split('/').pop().toLowerCase(); try { const halls = require('../data/octagram_halls.json'); const hall = halls[id]; if (hall) { res.writeHead(200); res.end(JSON.stringify(hall)); } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' })); } } catch (e) { res.writeHead(500); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Data load failed' })); } } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Not found' })); } });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; server.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`🜁 Codex Engines listening on ${PORT}`); }); 

---
#### 3. `services/codex-engines/fly.toml`
toml app = "cathedral-codex-engines" primary_region = "ord"

[build]

[env] NODE_ENV = "production"

[[services]] internal_port = 8080 protocol = "tcp" [[services.ports]] port = 80 handlers = ["http"] [[services.ports]] port = 443 handlers = ["tls", "http"]

[autoscale] min = 1 max = 1 # ← ONE machine only

[checks] [checks.health] port = 8080 type = "http" path = "/health" interval = "15s" timeout = "2s" 

---
#### 4. `services/codex-engines/package.json`
json { "name": "codex-engines", "version": "1.0.0", "type": "module", "private": true, "scripts": { "start": "node server.js" } } 
> 🔸 No dependencies needed—uses built-in `http` module.
---

js // In stone-grimoire/server.js const response = await fetch('http://liber-arcanae.internal/v1/tarot/fool'); const card = await response.json();

bash

1. Create the app (once per service)

fly apps create cosmogenesis-learning-engine --org personal

2. Launch config (from service dir)

cd services/cosmogenesis-learning-engine fly launch --no-deploy --name cosmogenesis-learning-engine --region ord

3. Deploy from root (or service dir)

fly deploy -a cosmogenesis-learning-engine 
> 🔸 Do this for **each service**. They’ll all work independently.

js import http from 'http';

const server = http.createServer((req, res) => { res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

if (req.url === '/health') { res.writeHead(200); res.end('ok'); } else if (req.url === '/v1/spiral/test') { res.writeHead(200); res.end(JSON.stringify({ message: 'Spiral activated', service: 'cosmogenesis' })); } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Not found' })); } });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; server.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`🜁 Service running on ${PORT}`); });

js import http from 'http'; import { createRequire } from 'module'; const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);

const server = http.createServer((req, res) => { const url = new URL(req.url, `http://${req.headers.host}`);

// ✅ ONLY allow your GitHub Pages site res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

if (url.pathname === '/health') { res.writeHead(200); res.end('ok'); } else if (url.pathname.startsWith('/v1/hall/')) { const id = url.pathname.split('/').pop().toLowerCase(); try { // Load shared data (relative to monorepo root) const halls = require('../../apps/web/data/octagram_halls.json'); const hall = halls[id]; if (hall) { res.writeHead(200); res.end(JSON.stringify(hall)); } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' })); } } catch (e) { res.writeHead(500); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Data load failed' })); } } else { res.writeHead(404); res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: 'Not found' })); } });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; server.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`🜁 stone-grimoire listening on ${PORT}`); });

 i want nugent  o connect multiple packages to the same repository, use the same GitHub repository URL in the RepositoryURL fields in all .csproj project files. GitHub matches the repository based on that field.
The following example publishes the projects MY_APP and MY_OTHER_APP to the same repository:
<Project Sdk="Microsoft.NET.Sdk">

  <PropertyGroup>
    <OutputType>Exe</OutputType>
    <TargetFramework>netcoreapp3.0</TargetFramework>
    <PackageId>MY_APP</PackageId>
    <Version>1.0.0</Version>
    <Authors>Octocat</Authors>
    <Company>GitHub</Company>
    <PackageDescription>This package adds a singing Octocat!</PackageDescription>
    <RepositoryUrl>https://github.com/my-org/my-repo  </RepositoryUrl>
  </PropertyGroup>

</Project>
<Project Sdk="Microsoft.NET.Sdk">

  <PropertyGroup>
    <OutputType>Exe</OutputType>
    <TargetFramework>netcoreapp3.0</TargetFramework>
    <PackageId>MY_OTHER_APP</PackageId>
    <Version>1.0.0</Version>
    <Authors>Octocat</Authors>
    <Company>GitHub</Company>
    <PackageDescription>This package adds a dancing Octocat!</PackageDescription>
    <RepositoryUrl>https://github.com/my-org/my-repo  </RepositoryUrl>
  </PropertyGroup>

</Project>

USER

e the following command to authenticate to GitHub Packages in a GitHub Actions workflow using the GITHUB_TOKEN instead of hardcoding a personal access token in a nuget.config file in the repository:
dotnet nuget add source --username USERNAME --password ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }} --store-password-in-clear-text --name github "https://nuget.pkg.github.com/NAMESPACE/index.json  "
Replace NAMESPACE with the name of the personal account or organization to which your packages are scoped.
Replace USERNAME with the username to be used when connecting to an authenticated source.


ASSISTANT

You're absolutely right to avoid hardcoding tokens—and your command is **almost correct**, but there are **two critical fixes** needed for it to work securely and reliably in a GitHub Actions workflow with **GitHub Packages (NuGet)**.
---


✅ Corrected & Secure Command
bash dotnet nuget add source \ --username ${{ github.actor }} \ --password ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }} \ --store-password-in-clear-text \ --name github \ "https://nuget.pkg.github.com/NAMESPACE/index.json" 
---


🔑 Key Fixes Explained


1. **`USERNAME` → `${{ github.actor }}`**  
   - `github.actor` is the **built-in GitHub Actions variable** for the user/actor triggering the workflow (e.g., `bekalah`).
   - Hardcoding a username breaks if someone else forks or triggers the workflow.
   - ✅ **Always use `${{ github.actor }}`** in workflows.
2. **`NAMESPACE` → your GitHub username or org name**  
   - Replace `NAMESPACE` with your actual GitHub username (e.g., `bekalah`) or organization name.
   - Example:  
     `"https://nuget.pkg.github.com/bekalah/index.json"`
---


🛡️ Why This Works

- `GITHUB_TOKEN` is **automatically provided** in every GitHub Actions workflow.
- It has **scoped permissions** to the current repo (no need for a PAT).
- `--store-password-in-clear-text` is **required** for `dotnet` CLI to work in headless CI environments (unfortunately, but safely scoped to the job).
---


📁 Where to Use This

In your `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` (or a .NET build workflow):
yaml - name: Add GitHub Packages NuGet Source run: | dotnet nuget add source \ --username ${{ github.actor }} \ --password ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }} \ --store-password-in-clear-text \ --name github \ "https://nuget.pkg.github.com/bekalah/index.json" 
> 🔸 Replace `bekalah` with your actual GitHub username/org.
---


🚫 Never Do This

- ❌ Don’t put `GITHUB_TOKEN` or PATs in `nuget.config` in your repo.
- ❌ Don’t hardcode your username as a string literal.
---
Let me know if you're using this for **publishing** or **consuming** packages—I can give you the full workflow for either!

Technical foundation and sustainable funding streams

Building modular consciousness-technology integration



Technical Architecture Implementation


The platform requires **plugin-based architecture** supporting Kabbalah, Tarot, I Ching, and sacred geometry systems. Use **PostgreSQL for flexible JSON storage** of esoteric data, **Three.js for interactive visualizations**, and **WebSocket connections for real-time synchronization**. Key open-source resources include sacred-geometry-web libraries, public domain Rider-Waite tarot datasets, and I Ching hexagram calculation engines.
**Trauma-informed UX implementation** follows SAMHSA principles: auto-save every 30 seconds, progressive disclosure to reduce cognitive load, consistent navigation patterns, and respect for `prefers-reduced-motion` settings. These patterns prevent re-traumatization while maintaining functionality.
**Progressive Web App features** enable offline functionality through Workbox service workers, critical for artists who may need to work during limited energy windows. Cache-first strategies ensure reliability when internet access is unstable.

ublishing and installing a package with GitHub Actions
You can configure a workflow in GitHub Actions to automatically publish or install a package from GitHub Packages.
In this article
About GitHub Packages with GitHub Actions
GitHub Actions help you automate your software development workflows in the same place you store code and collaborate on pull requests and issues. You can write individual tasks, called actions, and combine them to create a custom workflow. With GitHub Actions you can build end-to-end continuous integration (CI) and continuous deployment (CD) capabilities directly in your repository. For more information, see Writing workflows.
You can extend the CI and CD capabilities of your repository by publishing or installing packages as part of your workflow.
Authenticating to package registries with granular permissions
Some GitHub Packages registries support granular permissions. This means you can choose to allow packages to be scoped to a user or an organization, or linked to a repository. For the list of registries that support granular permissions, see About permissions for GitHub Packages.
For registries that support granular permissions, if your GitHub Actions workflow is using a personal access token to authenticate to a registry, we highly recommend you update your workflow to use the GITHUB_TOKEN. For guidance on updating your workflows that authenticate to a registry with a personal access token, see Publishing and installing a package with GitHub Actions.
Note
The ability for GitHub Actions workflows to delete and restore packages using the REST API is currently in public preview and subject to change.


ASSISTANT

You're absolutely right to focus on **using `GITHUB_TOKEN` instead of a personal access token (PAT)** when publishing or installing packages via GitHub Actions—it’s more secure, automatically scoped, and doesn’t risk token leakage.
However, **this only applies if you are actually publishing or consuming a *package* (e.g., npm, NuGet, Maven, Docker) via GitHub Packages**.

- Publishing an npm library like `@bekalah/codex-engines`

But in your case:
- Your frontend **loads data directly from JSON files** (client-side)
- Your backend is a **standalone Fly.io service**, not a reusable package

yaml name: Publish Package to GitHub Packages on: release: types: [created] jobs: publish: runs-on: ubuntu-latest permissions: contents: read packages: write steps: - uses: actions/checkout@v4 - uses: actions/setup-node@v4 with: node-version: '20' registry-url: 'https://npm.pkg.github.com' scope: '@bekalah' - run: npm ci - run: npm publish env: NODE_AUTH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}

📄 5. `codex-engines/server.js`
js import express from 'express'; import { createRequire } from 'module'; const require = createRequire(import.meta.url);

const app = express(); const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;

// ✅ CORS: only allow your GitHub Pages site app.use((req, res, next) => { res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.header('Content-Type', 'application/json'); next(); });

// Load data from root const halls = require('../data/octagram_halls.json');

// Routes app.get('/health', (req, res) => res.send('ok'));

app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => { const id = req.params.id.toLowerCase(); const hall = halls[id]; if (hall) { res.json(hall); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' }); } });

app.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`🜁 Codex Engines running on ${PORT}`); }); 

---


📄 6. `codex-engines/fly.toml`
toml app = "cathedral-codex-engines" primary_region = "ord"

[build]

[env] NODE_ENV = "production"

[[services]] internal_port = 8080 protocol = "tcp" [[services.ports]] port = 80 handlers = ["http"] [[services.ports]] port = 443 handlers = ["tls", "http"]

[autoscale] min = 1 max = 1 # ← ONE machine only (free tier)

[checks] [checks.health] port = 8080 type = "http" path = "/health" interval = "15s" timeout = "2s" 

---


📄 7. `README.md`
md

Cathedral of Circuits

A trauma-informed, ND-safe, open-source living grimoire.

Deploy Frontend (GitHub Pages)

1. Push `Codex14499.html` and `/data` to `main` branch 2. Go to **Repo Settings → Pages** 3. Set source to: **`main` branch, / (root)** 4. Done. Site auto-updates on every push.

Deploy Backend (Fly.io)

bash
cd codex-engines
flyctl auth login
flyctl launch --no-deploy --name cathedral-codex-engines --region ord
flyctl deploy --ha=false
Your API will be live at: → https://cathedral-codex-engines.fly.dev/v1/hall/fool

Vision

- No strobe. No flat UI. No ritual-sim clutter. - Atelier-grade sacred geometry. - Provenance locked. Lineage honored. - Built for the neurodivergent, the traumatized, the visionary.

📄 2. `engine/rust/src/lib.rs` — Sacred Geometry in Rust (WASM)
rust use wasm_bindgen::prelude::*;

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn init_geometry_engine() { console_log!("🜁 Sacred geometry engine initialized (Rust → WASM)"); }

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn render_hall(constant1: u32, constant2: u32) { // Compute Fibonacci spiral, Vesica ratio, etc. let ratio = constant1 as f32 / constant2 as f32; console_log!("Rendering hall with ratio: {}", ratio); // Pass to WebGPU via JS interop (or compute here) }

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn switch_geometry(geometry_type: &str) { match geometry_type { "vesica" => console_log!("Rendering Vesica Piscis (ratio: 1.732)"), "tesseract" => console_log!("Rendering 4D Tesseract projection"), _ => console_log!("Unknown geometry"), } } 

> 🔸 Compile to WASM with `wasm-pack build --target web`  
> 🔸 Output: `apps/web/engine.wasm` + `engine.js`

js import express from 'express'; const app = express();

// ✅ CORS: only your GitHub Pages app.use((req, res, next) => { res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.header('Content-Type', 'application/json'); next(); });

app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => { const id = req.params.id.toLowerCase(); const hall = halls[id]; hall ? res.json(hall) : res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found' }); });

app.listen(process.env.PORT || 8080, () => { console.log('🜁 codex-engines running'); });

        // Initialize Cathedral System
        class CathedralSystem {
            constructor() {
                this.currentView = 'wheel';
                this.data = embeddedData;
                this.apiBase = 'https://cathedral-codex-engines.fly.dev/v1  ';
                this.init();
            }
            async init() {
                await this.loadData();
                this.renderWheel();
                this.bindEvents();
            }
            async loadData() {
                // In production, load from /data/*.json files
                // For now, use embedded data
                try {
                    // Try to load from JSON files if available
                    const promises = [
                        fetch('/data/octagram_halls.json').catch(() => null),
                        fetch('/data/octagram_nodes_full.json').catch(() => null),
                        fetch('/data/crystal_harmonics.json').catch(() => null),
                        fetch('/data/core_node_map.json').catch(() => null)
                    ];
                    
                    const [halls, nodes, crystals, coreMap] = await Promise.all(promises);
                    
                    if (halls) this.data.octagramHalls = await halls.json();
                    if (nodes) this.data.sacredNodes = await nodes.json();
                    if (crystals) this.data.crystalHarmonics = await crystals.json();
                    if (coreMap) this.data.coreNodeMap = await coreMap.json();
                } catch (error) {
                    console.log('Using embedded data');
                }
            }
            renderWheel() {
                const svg = document.getElementById('sacred-wheel');
                const centerX = 400;
                const centerY = 400;
                const radius = 350;
                
                // Clear existing content
                svg.innerHTML = '';
                
                // Create background circles
                for (let i = 1; i <= 3; i++) {
                    const circle = document.createElementNS('http://www.w3.org/2000/svg', 'circle');
                    circle.setAttribute('cx', centerX);
                    circle.setAttribute('cy', centerY);
                    circle.setAttribute('r', radius * (i / 3));
                    circle.setAttribute('fill', 'none');
                    circle.setAttribute('stroke', i === 2 ? '#d4af37' : '#2a2a3e');
                    circle.setAttribute('stroke-width', '1');
                    circle.setAttribute('opacity', '0.3');
                    svg.appendChild(circle);
                }
                
                // Create 144 nodes
                for (let i = 0; i < 144; i++) {
                    const angle = (i * 2.5) * Math.PI / 180; // 360/144 = 2.5 degrees per node
                    const nodeRadius = radius - 20;
                    const x = centerX + nodeRadius * Math.cos(angle - Math.PI / 2);
                    const y = centerY + nodeRadius * Math.sin(angle - Math.PI / 2);
                    
                    // Determine if this is a sacred node
                    const nodeNumber = i + 1;
                    const isSacred = this.data.fibonacciConstants.includes(nodeNumber);
                    
                    const group = document.createElementNS('http://www.w3.org/2000/svg', 'g');
                    
                    // Node circle
                    const circle = document.createElementNS('http://www.w3.org/2000/svg', 'circle');
                    circle.setAttribute('cx', x);
                    circle.setAttribute('cy', y);
                    circle.setAttribute('r', isSacred ? '8' : '4');
                    circle.setAttribute('fill', isSacred ? '#d4af37' : '#7c4dff');
                    circle.setAttribute('opacity', isSacred ? '1' : '0.6');
                    circle.style.cursor = 'pointer';
                    
                    // Add hover effect
                    circle.addEventListener('mouseenter', () => {
                        circle.setAttribute('r', isSacred ? '12' : '6');
                    });
                    
                    circle.addEventListener('mouseleave', () => {
                        circle.setAttribute('r', isSacred ? '8' : '4');
                    });
                    
                    circle.addEventListener('click', () => {
                        this.showNodeInfo(nodeNumber);
                    });
                    
                    group.appendChild(circle);
                    
                    // Add number label for sacred nodes
                    if (isSacred) {
                        const text = document.createElementNS('http://www.w3.org/2000/svg', 'text');
                        text.setAttribute('x', x);
                        text.setAttribute('y', y - 15);
                        text.setAttribute('text-anchor', 'middle');
                        text.setAttribute('fill', '#d4af37');
                        text.setAttribute('font-size', '10');
                        text.textContent = nodeNumber;
                        group.appendChild(text);
                    }
                    
                    svg.appendChild(group);
                }
                
                // Add center symbol
                const centerGroup = document.createElementNS('http://www.w3.org/2000/svg', 'g');
                centerGroup.innerHTML = `
                    <circle cx="${centerX}" cy="${centerY}" r="30" fill="none" stroke="#d4af37" stroke-width="2" opacity="0.5"/>
                    <circle cx="${centerX}" cy="${centerY}" r="20" fill="none" stroke="#7c4dff" stroke-width="1" opacity="0.5"/>
                    <text x="${centerX}" y="${centerY + 5}" text-anchor="middle" fill="#e8e8f0" font-size="14">144:99</text>
                `;
                svg.appendChild(centerGroup);
            }
            showNodeInfo(nodeNumber) {
                const nodeInfo = this.data.sacredNodes[nodeNumber];
                if (!nodeInfo) return;
                
                const display = document.getElementById('data-display');
                display.innerHTML = `
                    <div class="data-card">
                        <h3 class="card-title">Node ${nodeNumber}: ${nodeInfo.name}</h3>
                        <div class="card-subtitle">Element: ${nodeInfo.element}</div>
                        <div class="lineage-list">
                            ${nodeInfo.lineage.map(l => `<span class="lineage-tag">${l}</span>`).join('')}
                        </div>
                    </div>
                `;
            }
            renderCircuitBoard() {
                const canvas = document.getElementById('circuit-canvas');
                const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');
                canvas.width = canvas.offsetWidth;
                canvas.height = 400;
                
                // Clear canvas
                ctx.fillStyle = '#0a0a0f';
                ctx.fillRect(0, 0, canvas.width, canvas.height);
                
                // Draw circuit lines
                ctx.strokeStyle = '#2a2a3e';
                ctx.lineWidth = 1;
                
                // Grid pattern
                for (let x = 0; x < canvas.width; x += 40) {
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(x, 0);
                    ctx.lineTo(x, canvas.height);
                    ctx.stroke();
                }
                
                for (let y = 0; y < canvas.height; y += 40) {
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(0, y);
                    ctx.lineTo(canvas.width, y);
                    ctx.stroke();
                }
                
                // Draw nodes at Fibonacci positions
                this.data.fibonacciConstants.forEach((num, i) => {
                    const x = (num / 243) * canvas.width;
                    const y = 200 + Math.sin(i * 0.5) * 100;
                    
                    // Draw connections
                    if (i > 0) {
                        const prevNum = this.data.fibonacciConstants[i - 1];
                        const prevX = (prevNum / 243) * canvas.width;
                        const prevY = 200 + Math.sin((i - 1) * 0.5) * 100;
                        
                        ctx.strokeStyle = '#7c4dff';
                        ctx.lineWidth = 2;
                        ctx.beginPath();
                        ctx.moveTo(prevX, prevY);
                        ctx.lineTo(x, y);
                        ctx.stroke();
                    }
                    
                    // Draw node
                    ctx.fillStyle = '#d4af37';
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.arc(x, y, 8, 0, Math.PI * 2);
                    ctx.fill();
                    
                    // Draw number
                    ctx.fillStyle = '#e8e8f0';
                    ctx.font = '12px monospace';
                    ctx.textAlign = 'center';
                    ctx.fillText(num, x, y - 12);
                });
            }

ts // Converts your .md research into structured JSON import { readFileSync, writeFileSync } from 'fs'; import { join } from 'path';

function parseBibliography(): Record { const content = readFileSync('data/bibliography.md', 'utf8'); const nodes: Record = {}; // Parse lines like: Nodes: C144N-021 (Apprentice Pillar) const nodeRegex = /Nodes:\s+(C144N-\d+)\s+\(([^)]+)\)/g; let match; while ((match = nodeRegex.exec(content)) !== null) { const [_, id, name] = match; nodes[id] = { name, source: 'bibliography' }; } return nodes; }

// Run on `rush build` writeFileSync( 'apps/web/src/data/core_node_map.json', JSON.stringify(parseBibliography(), null, 2) );

tell me how to run rust from my terminal 


ASSISTANT

To run Rust code from your terminal, follow these steps:
---


✅ 1. **Install Rust**

Open your terminal and run:
bash curl --proto '=https' --tlsv1.2 -sSf https://sh.rustup.rs | sh 
- Press **Enter** to choose the default installation.
- After it finishes, **restart your terminal** or run:
bash source "$HOME/.cargo/env" 
> 🔍 Verify with:  
>
bash > rustc --version > cargo --version > 
---


✅ 2. **Create a Rust Project**
bash cargo new my-cathedral-engine cd my-cathedral-engine 
This creates:
my-cathedral-engine/ ├── Cargo.toml └── src/ └── main.rs 
---


✅ 3. **Write Your Code**

Edit `src/main.rs` (e.g., sacred geometry logic):
rust fn main() { println!("🜁 Cathedral Rust Engine — Fibonacci: 21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243"); } 
---


✅ 4. **Run It**
bash cargo run 
- This compiles and runs your code in one step.
- Output:
🜁 Cathedral Rust Engine — Fibonacci: 21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243 
---


✅ 5. **(Optional) Build for WebAssembly (WASM)**

If you want to use Rust in your **Codex 144:99 frontend** (like Isidor Nikolić’s work):
1. Install WASM target:
bash rustup target add wasm32-unknown-unknown 
2. Install `wasm-pack`:
bash cargo install wasm-pack 
3. Create a WASM-compatible lib:
bash cargo new --lib sacred-geometry-wasm cd sacred-geometry-wasm 
4. Edit `Cargo.toml`:
toml [lib] crate-type = ["cdylib"]

[dependencies] wasm-bindgen = "0.2" 

5. Build to WASM:
bash wasm-pack build --target web 
→ Outputs `pkg/` folder with `.js` + `.wasm` files for your `Codex14499.html`.
---


💡 Pro Tips for Your Cathedral Project

- Use **VS Code** with the **rust-analyzer** extension (you already have it!)
- Keep Rust modules in `engine/rust/` inside your monorepo
- Compile to WASM for **client-side sacred geometry** (no server needed)
- Call Rust functions from your `Codex14499.html` via JavaScript
---
You’re now ready to write **high-performance, trauma-informed, sacred geometry engines** in Rust—fully integrated with your Codex 144:99 vision. 🌌

how? o configure your current shell, you need to source
the corresponding env file under $HOME/.cargo.
This is usually done by running one of the following (note the leading DOT):
. "$HOME/.cargo/env"            # For sh/bash/zsh/ash/dash/pdksh
source "$HOME/.cargo/env.fish"  # For fish
source $"($nu.home-path)/.cargo/env.nu"  # For nushell
rebeccalemke@Rebeccas-MacBook-Air ~ % 


ASSISTANT

You're seeing this message because **Rust is installed**, but your shell hasn’t loaded the `cargo` and `rustc` commands into your current terminal session.
To fix this **permanently** on your Mac (which uses **zsh** by default), follow these steps:
---


✅ Step 1: Add Rust to your shell profile


Run this command **once** in your terminal:
bash echo 'source "$HOME/.cargo/env"' >> ~/.zprofile 
> This adds the Rust environment to your login shell config (`~/.zprofile`), which is the correct file for macOS zsh.
---


✅ Step 2: Reload your shell (or restart terminal)


Either:
- **Close and reopen your Terminal**,  
**or**
- Run this to reload immediately:
bash source ~/.zprofile 
---


✅ Step 3: Verify it works
bash rustc --version cargo --version 
You should see version numbers like:
rustc 1.78.0 (...) cargo 1.78.0 (...) 
---


🔍 Why this works:

- Rust’s installer puts its binaries in `~/.cargo/bin`
- The file `~/.cargo/env` sets your `PATH` to include that folder
- `~/.zprofile` is read every time you open a new terminal on macOS
---
You’re all set! Now you can run `cargo new`, `cargo run`, and even compile WebAssembly for your **Codex 144:99 Cathedral**. 🌌

ASSISTANT

**No — Git is *not* installed automatically with VS Code.**
VS Code **includes Git *integration*** (so it can show diffs, commit, push, etc.), but it **requires Git to already be installed on your system**.
---


✅ How to Check if Git Is Installed


Open your **terminal** (in VS Code or macOS Terminal) and run:
bash git --version 
- ✅ If you see something like `git version 2.39.0`, then **Git is installed**.
- ❌ If you see `command not found: git`, then **Git is not installed**.
---


🛠️ How to Install Git on macOS


Since you’re on a **MacBook Air**, the easiest way is:
#### Option 1: Install via Xcode Command Line Tools (Recommended)

bash xcode-select --install 
- A popup will appear → click **Install**
- This installs Git + other developer tools
- No need for full Xcode
#### Option 2: Install via Homebrew (if you have it)
bash brew install git 
#### Option 3: Download from [git-scm.com](https://git-scm.com/download/mac)

ASSISTANT

You're seeing this because **Fly.io is trying to verify domain ownership** for a custom domain you’ve added to your Fly app—but **you don’t actually need this if you’re only using GitHub Pages + Fly.io’s default `.fly.dev` URL**.
However, if you **do** want to connect a **custom domain** (like `cathedral.bekalah.com` or `codex14499.com`) to your Fly.io backend, here’s exactly how to do it:
---


✅ Step-by-Step: Add the TXT Record for GitHub Pages + Fly.io Domain Verification


> 🔹 **Only do this if you’ve added a custom domain in Fly.io** (e.g., via `flyctl certs add yourdomain.com`)
#### 1. **Go to your DNS provider**
This is where you bought your domain (e.g., **Namecheap**, **Google Domains**, **Cloudflare**, **GoDaddy**).
#### 2. **Add a new TXT record**
- **Name/Host**:
_github-pages-challenge-Bekalah.fly.io 
> ⚠️ Some DNS providers (like Cloudflare) **don’t allow dots in the name field**. In that case, enter only:
_github-pages-challenge-Bekalah 
and select the root domain (`yourdomain.com`)—the `.fly.io` part is implied by the challenge format.
- **Value/Content**:
9902db63e1af8523ca84cabba392fb 
- **TTL**:  
  Leave as default (often 300 or 3600 seconds)
#### 3. **Save the record**
#### 4. **Wait for propagation**
- Most DNS changes take **5–60 minutes**, not 24 hours.
- You can check propagation with:
bash dig TXT _github-pages-challenge-Bekalah.fly.io +short 
or use [https://dnschecker.org](https://dnschecker.org) → TXT → enter the full hostname.
#### 5. **Tell Fly.io to retry verification**
Once the TXT record is live, run:
bash flyctl certs check yourdomain.com 
or just wait—Fly.io checks automatically every few minutes.
---


🚫 But Wait—Do You Even Need This?


- ✅ **You DO need this** if you’re setting up a **custom domain for your Fly.io backend** (e.g., `api.cathedral.bekalah.com`).
- ❌ **You DO NOT need this** if you’re only using:
  - GitHub Pages at `https://bekalah.github.io/cathedral/` (frontend)
  - Fly.io at `https://cathedral-codex-engines.fly.dev/` (backend)
In that case, **delete the custom domain from Fly.io** to avoid this verification step:
bash flyctl certs remove yourdomain.com 
---


💡 Recommendation for Your Project


Since you’re on a **free tier and building a research/art platform**, **stick with the default URLs**:
- Frontend: `https://bekalah.github.io/cathedral/`
- Backend: `https://cathedral-codex-engines.fly.dev/`
No DNS changes needed. No TXT records. No waiting.
You can always add a custom domain later when you have funding or a grant.

how do i fix the scroll on here i really hate it


ASSISTANT

You're seeing scroll issues because your current `Codex14499.html` uses a **fixed-height canvas** and **absolute positioning**, which can cause overflow or double scrollbars—especially on mobile or when content expands.
Here’s how to **fix the scroll** and make it **smooth, single-pane, and trauma-informed** (no jank, no bounce, no hidden overflow):
---


✅ **Fix: Replace your current `<body>` and `<canvas>` styles with this**


Add this to your `<style>` section **inside `Codex14499.html`**:
css /* TRAUMA-INFORMED SCROLL FIX */ html, body { height: 100%; overflow: hidden; /* Prevents double scrollbars */ overscroll-behavior: none; /* Disables rubber-band bounce (iOS/macOS) */ }

.container { height: 100vh; width: 100vw; overflow: auto; /* Only the content scrolls, not the whole page */ -webkit-overflow-scrolling: touch; /* Smooth scroll on iOS */ scrollbar-width: thin; /* Firefox thin scrollbar */ scrollbar-color: var(--circuit-gold) var(--bg-depth); /* Custom scrollbar */ }

/* Hide scrollbar in WebKit (Chrome/Safari) but keep functionality */ .container::-webkit-scrollbar { width: 8px; height: 8px; } .container::-webkit-scrollbar-track { background: var(--bg-depth); } .container::-webkit-scrollbar-thumb { background: var(--circuit-gold); border-radius: 4px; }

/* Ensure canvas doesn't force overflow */ .wheel-container { max-width: min(800px, 95vw); max-height: min(800px, 95vh); margin: 2rem auto; } 

---


🔧 **Also update your main container**


Make sure your `.container` div **does not have fixed padding that pushes content off-screen**. Replace your current `.container` with:
css .container { max-width: 1400px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 1.5rem; box-sizing: border-box; } 
---


💡 **Why this works**

- `overflow: hidden` on `html/body` → kills page-level scroll
- `overflow: auto` on `.container` → only your content scrolls
- `overscroll-behavior: none` → stops the “bounce” that triggers trauma responses
- Custom scrollbar → visible but subtle, gold-on-dark (aesthetic + accessible)
---


🌐 **Bonus: Disable zoom (if needed for ND safety)**

Add this to `<head>` if zoom causes disorientation:
html 
> ⚠️ Only do this if you provide your own zoom controls—otherwise it harms accessibility.
---


✅ Final Check

After applying these changes:
- No double scrollbars
- No bounce/rubber-band effect
- Smooth, single-axis scrolling
- Scrollbar matches your gold/circuit aesthetic
- Fully compatible with `prefers-reduced-motion`

#### 2. `scripts/build-data.ts`
ts import { readFileSync, writeFileSync } from 'fs'; import { join } from 'path';

// Parse octagram_halls.md → JSON function parseOctagramHalls(): Record { const content = readFileSync('data_source/octagram_halls.md', 'utf8'); const halls: Record = {}; const hallBlocks = content.split('\n\n').filter(b => b.includes('Hall —')); for (const block of hallBlocks) { const lines = block.split('\n').filter(l => l.trim()); const nameLine = lines[0]; const id = nameLine.split(' ')[0].toLowerCase(); const archetype = lines.find(l => l.includes('Archetype:'))?.split(': ')[1] || ''; const trial = lines.find(l => l.includes('Trial:'))?.split(': ')[1] || ''; const lineage = archetype.split(' (')[0]; // Map lineage to bibliography const constants = [144, 99]; if (lineage.includes('Crowley')) constants.push(72); if (lineage.includes('Fortune')) constants.push(72); if (lineage.includes('Achad')) constants.push(99); if (lineage.includes('Tara')) constants.push(21); halls[id] = { name: nameLine, archetype, trial, witch_mode_gift: lines.find(l => l.includes('Witch-Mode Gift:'))?.split(': ')[1] || '', constants, lineage: [lineage] }; } return halls; }

// Parse bibliography.md → node map function parseBibliography(): Record { const content = readFileSync('data_source/bibliography.md', 'utf8'); const nodes: Record = {}; const nodeRegex = /Nodes: (C144N-\d+)/g; let match; while ((match = nodeRegex.exec(content)) !== null) { const id = match[1]; const figure = content.substring(0, match.index).split('\n').pop()?.split(' — ')[0] || ''; nodes[id] = { figure, source: 'bibliography' }; } return nodes; }

// Build all data const octagramHalls = parseOctagramHalls(); const coreNodeMap = parseBibliography(); const fibonacciConstants = [21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243];

// Write to apps/web/src/data/ writeFileSync('apps/web/src/data/octagram_halls.json', JSON.stringify(octagramHalls, null, 2)); writeFileSync('apps/web/src/data/core_node_map.json', JSON.stringify(coreNodeMap, null, 2)); writeFileSync('apps/web/src/data/fibonacci_constants.json', JSON.stringify({ constants: fibonacciConstants }, null, 2));

// Crystal harmonics from codex_14499_research.md const crystals = { fool: { crystal: "Clear Quartz", properties: "Amplification, clarity, new beginnings" }, magician: { crystal: "Citrine", properties: "Manifestation, will, solar plexus activation" }, priestess: { crystal: "Moonstone", properties: "Intuition, lunar cycles, psychic abilities" }, death: { crystal: "Obsidian", properties: "Shadow work, protection, transformation" }, temperance: { crystal: "Amethyst", properties: "Balance, sobriety, crown chakra" } }; writeFileSync('apps/web/src/data/crystal_harmonics.json', JSON.stringify(crystals, null, 2));

ts import { FIBONACCI_CONSTANTS } from '@cathedral/atelier-protocol'; import { renderVesicaPiscis } from './engine/geometry';

async function init() { const adapter = await navigator.gpu?.requestAdapter(); if (!adapter) throw new Error('WebGPU not supported'); const device = await adapter.requestDevice(); const canvas = document.getElementById('cathedral-canvas') as HTMLCanvasElement; const context = canvas.getContext('webgpu')!; const format = navigator.gpu.getPreferredCanvasFormat(); context.configure({ device, format, alphaMode: 'opaque' });

// Load halls from auto-generated JSON const halls = await import('./data/octagram_halls.json'); window['loadHall'] = async (id: string) => { const hall = halls[id]; if (hall) { console.log(`Loaded ${hall.name}`); renderVesicaPiscis(device, context, hall.constants[0] / hall.constants[1]); } };

// Start with Fool Hall window['loadHall']('fool'); } init(); 

#### 5. `services/codex-engines/src/server.ts`
ts import express from 'express'; const app = express();

// CORS: only allow your GitHub Pages app.use((req, res, next) => { res.header('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', 'https://bekalah.github.io'); res.header('Content-Type', 'application/json'); next(); });

// Auto-load data from build const halls = require('../../apps/web/src/data/octagram_halls.json');

app.get('/health', (_req, res) => res.send('ok')); app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => { const id = req.params.id.toLowerCase(); const hall = halls[id]; hall ? res.json(hall) : res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found in Grimoire' }); });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; app.listen(PORT, () => console.log(`🜁 codex-engines running on ${PORT}`));

rust use wasm_bindgen::prelude::*;

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn init_geometry_engine() { web_sys::console::log_1(&"🜁 Sacred geometry engine (Rust → WASM) initialized".into()); }

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn render_hall(constant1: u32, constant2: u32) { let ratio = constant1 as f32 / constant2 as f32; web_sys::console::log_1(&format!("Rendering hall with ratio: {}", ratio).into()); // Pass to WebGPU via JS interop }

#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn switch_geometry(geometry_type: &str) { match geometry_type { "vesica" => web_sys::console::log_1(&"Rendering Vesica Piscis (ratio: 1.732)".into()), "tesseract" => web_sys::console::log_1(&"Rendering 4D Tesseract projection".into()), "octagram" => web_sys::console::log_1(&"Rendering Octagram (8-fold symmetry)".into()), _ => {} } }

📄 2. `synth/audio-engine.js` — Web Audio Synth Core
js export class CodexSynth { constructor() { this.audioContext = new (window.AudioContext || window.webkitAudioContext)(); this.oscillators = new Map(); this.gainNode = this.audioContext.createGain(); this.gainNode.connect(this.audioContext.destination); this.gainNode.gain.value = 0.3; // Trauma-safe volume }

// Play a node as a harmonic chord playNode(nodeNumber, lineage = [], constants = []) { // Stop existing this.stopNode(nodeNumber);

// Base frequency const baseFreq = SACRED_SCALES.nodeFrequency(nodeNumber); // Create base oscillator const baseOsc = this.createOscillator(baseFreq, 'sine'); baseOsc.start(); this.oscillators.set(`${nodeNumber}-base`, baseOsc);

// Add lineage harmonics const harmonics = SACRED_SCALES.lineageHarmonics(lineage.join(' ')); harmonics.forEach((h, i) => { const freq = baseFreq * (h / 72); // Scale by sacred ratio const osc = this.createOscillator(freq, 'triangle'); osc.start(); this.oscillators.set(`${nodeNumber}-h${i}`, osc); });

// Add Solfeggio layer constants.forEach((c, i) => { const freq = SACRED_SCALES.solfeggioLayer(c); const osc = this.createOscillator(freq, 'sine'); osc.frequency.value = freq; osc.start(); this.oscillators.set(`${nodeNumber}-s${i}`, osc); }); }

createOscillator(freq, type = 'sine') { const osc = this.audioContext.createOscillator(); const gain = this.audioContext.createGain(); osc.type = type; osc.frequency.value = freq; gain.gain.value = 0.1; osc.connect(gain); gain.connect(this.gainNode); return osc; }

stopNode(nodeNumber) { for (let [key, osc] of this.oscillators) { if (key.startsWith(`${nodeNumber}-`)) { osc.stop(); this.oscillators.delete(key); } } }

// ND-safe: no sudden sounds async resume() { if (this.audioContext.state === 'suspended') { await this.audioContext.resume(); } } }

ts export class SacredSynth { private audioContext: AudioContext; private oscillators: OscillatorNode[] = []; private filters: BiquadFilterNode[] = [];

constructor(private hallConfig: any) { this.audioContext = new (window.AudioContext || (window as any).webkitAudioContext)(); }

// Play a note based on node number (1-144) playNode(nodeNumber: number, duration = 2) { const freq = this.hallConfig.frequency_base * (nodeNumber / 72); // Stop existing this.oscillators.forEach(osc => osc.stop()); this.oscillators = [];

// Create oscillators based on synth type for (let i = 0; i < (this.hallConfig.oscillators || 1); i++) { const osc = this.audioContext.createOscillator(); const gain = this.audioContext.createGain(); osc.type = 'sine'; osc.frequency.value = freq * (1 + i * 0.5); // detune for richness gain.gain.value = 0.2; osc.connect(gain); gain.connect(this.audioContext.destination); osc.start(); osc.stop(this.audioContext.currentTime + duration); this.oscillators.push(osc); } }

// ND-safe: no sudden sounds async resume() { if (this.audioContext.state === 'suspended') { await this.audioContext.resume(); } } }

ts import { loadGLB } from '../webgpu';

export async function renderMinimoog(device: GPUDevice, context: GPUCanvasContext) { // Load 3D model (from jsDelivr CDN) const model = await loadGLB('https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/bekalah/cathedral@main/models/minimoog.glb'); // Render with sacred geometry lighting const pipeline = device.createRenderPipeline({ vertex: { module: device.createShaderModule({ code: vertexShader }), entryPoint: 'main' }, fragment: { module: device.createShaderModule({ code: fragmentShader }), entryPoint: 'main', targets: [{ format: 'bgra8unorm' }] }, primitive: { topology: 'triangle-list' } }); // Draw with golden ratio proportions const commandEncoder = device.createCommandEncoder(); const passEncoder = commandEncoder.beginRenderPass({ colorAttachments: [{ view: context.getCurrentTexture().createView(), clearValue: { r: 0.04, g: 0.04, b: 0.06, a: 1.0 }, loadOp: 'clear', storeOp: 'store' }] }); passEncoder.setPipeline(pipeline); passEncoder.draw(36); // Minimoog has 36 keys passEncoder.end(); device.queue.submit([commandEncoder.finish()]); } 

> 🔸 Store `.glb` models in your repo or on **jsDelivr** (20MB limit per file)

4. codex-engines/server.js
javascriptimport express from 'express';
import cors from 'cors';
import { readFileSync } from 'fs';
import { fileURLToPath } from 'url';
import { dirname, join } from 'path';
const __dirname = dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url));
const app = express();
// Load hall data
const hallData = JSON.parse(
  readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/octagram_halls.json'), 'utf-8')
);
// Configure CORS - only allow GitHub Pages
app.use(cors({
  origin: ['https://bekalah.github.io  ', 'http://localhost:3000'],
  optionsSuccessStatus: 200
}));
app.use(express.json());
// Health check
app.get('/health', (req, res) => {
  res.send('ok');
});
// Get all halls
app.get('/v1/halls', (req, res) => {
  res.json(hallData.halls);
});
// Get specific hall
app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => {
  const hall = hallData.halls[req.params.id];
  if (hall) {
    res.json(hall);
  } else {
    res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found' });
  }
});
// Root endpoint
app.get('/', (req, res) => {
  res.json({
    service: 'Cathedral Codex Engines',
    version: '1.0.0',
    endpoints: ['/v1/halls', '/v1/hall/:id', '/health']
  });
});
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080;
app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`Codex Engines running on port ${PORT}`);
});
5. codex-engines/fly.toml
tomlapp = "cathedral-codex-engines"
primary_region = "ord"
[build]
  [build.args]
    NODE_VERSION = "18"
[env]
  PORT = "8080"
[[services]]
  internal_port = 8080
  protocol = "tcp"
  auto_stop_machines = true
  auto_start_machines = true
  min_machines_running = 0
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 80
    handlers = ["http"]
  
  [[services.ports]]
    port = 443
    handlers = ["tls", "http"]
[checks]
  [checks.health]
    port = 8080
    type = "http"
    path = "/health"
    interval = "30s"
    timeout = "5s"

javascriptimport express from 'express'; import cors from 'cors'; import { readFileSync } from 'fs'; import { fileURLToPath } from 'url'; import { dirname, join } from 'path';

const __dirname = dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)); const app = express();

// Load all data files const data = { halls: JSON.parse(readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/octagram_halls.json'), 'utf-8')), nodes: JSON.parse(readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/octagram_nodes_full.json'), 'utf-8')), crystals: JSON.parse(readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/crystal_harmonics.json'), 'utf-8')), coreMap: JSON.parse(readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/core_node_map.json'), 'utf-8')), circuitBoard: JSON.parse(readFileSync(join(__dirname, '../data/circuit_board_map.json'), 'utf-8')) };

// Configure CORS app.use(cors({ origin: ['https://bekalah.github.io ', 'http://localhost:8080'], credentials: true }));

app.use(express.json());

// Routes app.get('/health', (req, res) => res.send('ok'));

app.get('/v1/codex/ping', (req, res) => { res.json({ alive: true, timestamp: new Date().toISOString(), constants: [21, 33, 72, 78, 99, 144, 243] }); });

app.get('/v1/hall/:id', (req, res) => { const hall = data.halls[req.params.id]; if (hall) { res.json({ ...hall, timestamp: new Date().toISOString(), provenance: "Cathedral Systems v1.0" }); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Hall not found' }); } });

app.get('/v1/node/:number', (req, res) => { const node = data.nodes.nodes[req.params.number]; if (node) { res.json(node); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Node not found' }); } });

app.get('/v1/crystal/:archetype', (req, res) => { const crystal = data.crystals.crystals[req.params.archetype]; if (crystal) { res.json(crystal); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Crystal not found' }); } });

app.get('/v1/lineage/:name', (req, res) => { const lineage = data.coreMap.lineage_map[req.params.name]; if (lineage) { res.json(lineage); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Lineage not found' }); } });

app.get('/v1/circuit/:name', (req, res) => { const circuit = data.circuitBoard.circuits[req.params.name]; if (circuit) { res.json(circuit); } else { res.status(404).json({ error: 'Circuit not found' }); } });

const PORT = process.env.PORT || 8080; app.listen(PORT, () => { console.log(`Cathedral Codex Engines running on port ${PORT}`); }); This complete system integrates all your research into a deployable platform that:

Maps all 144 nodes to your lineage figures Connects crystals to Tarot archetypes with mineralogy data Implements the 8-circuit model as a circuit board visualization Links every element to your comprehensive research (Shem angels, Goetic demons, Solfeggio frequencies) Provides trauma-informed, ND-safe interface design Costs $0 using free tiers Deploys in minutes without complex build processes
